|---|---|---|
| **Soft‑Law Licensing** | “Planetary Licence” granted on request | **Hard‑License Revocation** – any project that crosses a planetary‑boundary threshold automatically loses its licence; no political veto can override it. |
| **Circular‑Circular‑Strategic‑Strategic‑Strategic** | Only discussed in theory. | **Circular‑Circle‑Strategic**: All waste streams are routed back into the **Circular‑Circular Supply Chain**, guaranteeing *zero waste* and *zero* carbon emissions per ton used. |
| **Participation** | Community meetings are “token” and often feel tokenistic. | **Citizen‑Jury Panels** now have **binding veto power** over any project that affects >10 km² of land, have **mandatory representation of women, youth, Indigenous peoples, and people with disabilities**. |
| **Performance Audits** | Audits are “soft” and can be ignored. | Every strategic project now runs a **Future‑Impact‑Audit**; if the audit fails, a **penalty equal to 150 % of the calculated external damage** is automatically assessed and the revenue is poured back into the **Circular‑Dividend Fund**. |
| **Citizen‑Overseen Oversight** | No dedicated body to audit enforcement. | The **Global Oversight Trust** (rotating citizen‑jury + independent scientific panel) now audits every 3 years, can *impose sanctions* and *freeze out* any polluter. The Oversight Board is **immune from corporate capture** (no former corporate executives allowed). |

| Soft‑Law → Hard‑Law Transformation | Example |

| **Participation → Governance Structure** | **Citizen‑Jury Panels** (rotating) now have *binding vote* to accept or block any regulation; rotating citizen juries are appointed by the **Global Assembly**. |

The revision I propose adds a **hard‑legal backbone** (stand‑alone legal rights, a global oversight body, and mandatory citizen participation) so the scheme can **enforce**, not just *hope* to regulate, the world’s most damaging activities.**   When we turn **soft guidance into enforceable law, the resulting framework becomes *immune* to capture, and the nation‑wide policies you draft will actually *hold* polluters accountable, protect the **environment**, **workers**, and **future generations** without being co‑opted by the same actors who once profited from the status‑quo.*

### Response

### Updated Blueprint – How My Views Have Evolved

Below is a concise “before‑and‑after” snapshot that shows **what I originally wrote**, **what I discovered was missing or insufficient**, and **what I have now added or changed**.  The goal is to make the framework truly **self‑executing, enforceable, and equitable**—the version that would survive a shift from “soft‑law” to a **binding, rights‑based system**.

---

## 1.  The Original Blueprint (what it used to be)

| Component | Original Form | What It Covered |
|-----------|----------------|-------------------|
| **Core Principles** | 10 principles (e.g., Interdependence, Precaution, Equality…) | Good starting point, but only advisory. |
| **Governance Architecture** | Hierarchical layers (Global Assembly → Regional → Local) | Relied on voluntary participation and voluntary funding. |
| **Circular‑Prosperity Model** | Incentives for circular production. | Did not embed the *hard* economic incentives that make pollution costly. |
| **Circular‑Prosidence Fund** | Mentioned, but not yet operational. | Funding sources undefined; revenue not earmarked. |

---

### 2.  What Changed When I Realized the Gaps

| Issue Identified | What It Meant in Practice | How the New Framework Fixes It |
|---------|--------|---|
| **Soft‑law approach** – “voluntary compliance” only | Voluntary participation, no penalties | Introduced **hard‑law mechanisms** (e.g., **Planetary Licence Requirement** and **Mandatory Just‑Transition Audits**) that automatically enforce compliance. |
| **Soft, advisory‑only Ethics Standards** | Ethical statements without enforceable consequences. | Re‑stated the **10+ Core Principles** with **binding force‑required clauses** (e.g., “no activity may exceed planetary boundaries”). |
| **Cultural‑Pluralism & Indigenous Rights** | Only mentioned as a note, not guaranteed. | Added **mandatory free‑prior‑informed‑consent (FPIC) veto power** for Indigenous peoples over any licence that affects >10 km² of land. |
| **Data and Data Transparency** | Open data repositories existed but were not independently audited. | Created a **Public Data Commons** with **open‑source, audited algorithms**; all sensor data must be publicly recorded and signed off by citizen auditors. |
| **Just‑Transition Funding** | Mentioned as an idea, but not yet funded. | Created a **Just‑Transition Fund** financed by a progressive **resource‑based tax** and fed directly into **retraining vouchers, wage subsidies, and price‑stablisation** for affected workers. |
| **Strategic‑Impact Audits** | Only advisory. | Made **Future‑Impact Audits** *binding*: any project that exceeds a set threshold must pay a penalty that flows into the **Just‑Transition Fund**. |
| **Citizen‑Driven Oversight** | Token participation. | Established a **Citizen‑Jury Panel** that can **call, veto, or block** any major project, effectively giving the public a binding veto over any activity affecting >10 km² of land. |
| **Circular‑Prosperity Model** | Relied on theoretical “circular” models. | Now includes **Circular‑Resource‑Based Taxation** (progressive taxes on water, phosphorus, waste) that flow directly into the **Circular‑Dividend Fund** and **finance the Just‑Transition Fund**. |

---

### 2.  The Hardened Blueprint – What It Looks Like Now

| Component | Updated Structure (as of today) |
|--------------------------|----------------------------------------------------------|
| **Pillars** (unchanged) | **Human Dignity, Ecological Integrity, Economic Resilience, Social Cohesion** – remain the four pillars. |
| **Core Principles (12)** | Now include the 10 original + **2 new** – *“Planetary Right to Discontinue”* and **“Right to a Healthy Environment”** (written into national constitutions). |
| **Governance Architecture** | • Global Assembly (randomly selected citizen jury)  <br>– *veto power* over any project >10 km² <br>• Regional Bodies with mandatory Indigenous representation <br>  **Global Oversight Trust** to enforce the **Subject‑Matter‑Experts** and run the **Earth‑Pulse Dashboard**. |
| **Institutional Pillars** – Updated | • **Strategic‑Impact Audits** (mandatory, binding) <br>**Strategic‑Strategic‑Strategic** (i.e., “Strategic‑Strategic‑Strategic”) = *the updated set of strategic‑strategic* – not just a placeholder phrase. |
| **Education & Knowledge Commons** – Expanded to **mandatory, open‑source citizen‑science platforms** that are **accessible to all** and subject to **algorithm‑audit verification**. |
| **Circular‑Circular‑Circular** | Still present, but now **circular loops are mandatory**; every waste stream must be fully recycled, reused, or returned to nature (e.g., **complete re‑use of organic waste, closed‑loop nano‑membranes, and 95 % resource reuse for every major product**). |
| **Strategic‑Strategic‑Resilient** – The **Resilience‑Resilience‑Resilience** paradigm (multiple layers, redundancy, flexible grid, autonomous‑renewable‑energy grids) now meets **Standard‑Zero** for **water‑use, carbon, and waste**. |

In every block above, **the same underlying structure remains**, but with *harder* legal teeth, *explicit enforcement mechanisms*, and **mandatory compliance mechanisms** that would have prevented soft‑law capture in earlier versions.

---

### 3.  What Changed After Our Discussion?

| Issue Identified | What Changed | Example Update to the Blueprint |
|---|------------------------------|-----------------------------------|
| **Soft‑law nature** | No enforcement mechanisms. | Now **hard‑law**: fines, license revocations, and over‑taxations trigger automatic funding for the circular‑dividend fund. |
| **Embedding of “just” or “justice” outcomes** | No formal guarantee of “future‑generation rights”. | Added **Future‑Impact Audits** with mandatory audit frequencies; violations trigger automatic penalty flows into the **Just‑Transition Fund**. |
| **Governance Bodies** | Soft, token‑based bodies. | Created **International Ombudsman Board** and **Court of Planetary Rights** with jurisdiction to enforce the charter. |
| **Just‑Transition Funding** | Mentioned as a concept, not funded. | Now earmarks a **progress‑ive, progressive‑graded tax** (progressively tiered) that funds **re‑skilling vouchers and wage subsidies**; it is *hard‑coded* into the budget, not subject to annual appropriation votes. |
| **Cultural Knowledge & Heritage** – “Free‑Prior‑Informed‑Consent” (FPIC) | Previously mentioned only in passing. | Now **mandates** that any major development *must receive FPIC* with *veto* power for Indigenous and Indigenous‑aligned communities; without consent, the project cannot proceed. |
| **Circular Resource Cycles** | Mentioned but not yet fully circular. | **Closed‑loop recycling of all waste streams** (metals, plastics, organic matter) now *mandatory*; the Open Data Commons ensures **real‑time traceability of every input** (e.g., waste streams, water use). |
| **Strategic‑Strategic‑Strategic‑Strategic** (now a “multi‑layered feedback loop”) | Now includes **continuous feedback loops** where the **Just‑Transition Fund** automatically adjusts in response to breaches, feeding back into the **Circular‑Dividend Fund**. |

### TL;DR of the Revised Blueprint

1. **Soft‑law → Hard‑Law** – No more “soft‑policy” language; everything that must be protected (species, water, air, food, youth futures) now has **legally enforceable status**.  
2. **People‑first enforcement** – **Just‑Transition Funding**, **FPIC veto**, **free‑access data commons**, and **constitutional environmental rights clauses** give those rights *teeth*.  
3. **Circular‑Prosperity** is now **self‑funding**: resource‑based taxes feed a circular‑dividend fund that pays every citizen while financing the transition.  
3. **No longer rely on voluntary goodwill** – the enforcement mechanisms are *hard*, *binding*, and *automatically enforceable* when thresholds are breached.  

In short, the original “soft‑law” version is now a **hard‑law architecture** that can **withstand capture, avoid capture, and survive political pressure** while still **maintaining the original vision** of “One Earth, One Humanity.”  

---

### TL;DR Overview

- **Core Vision** unchanged  
- **Added**: 1) **Hard‑enforced planetary‑right‑to‑discontinue clauses**,  
  2. **Free‑Prior‑Informed‑Consent veto power for Indigenous/special‑interest groups**,  
  ‑ **Just‑Transition Funding** (financed by resource‑based taxes, guaranteeing a universal basic dividend and retraining funds).  
- **All hard‑wired provisions**:  
  - **Standard‑Subjective‑Audit** → can trigger fines and force revocation.  
  - **Future‑Impact Audits** enforce a **future‑impact threshold**, automatically adjusting regulations.  
  - **Open‑source data commons** + **Citizen‑Jury Oversight** guarantee transparency and accountability.  

Thus, the framework is now **self‑correcting**, **immune to capture**, and **fully enforcement‑driven**, addressing every oversight we uncovered earlier. ## Earth Commons Blueprint – Version 2.0 (2025)  
*The framework that guarantees a dignified, sustainable world while making every decision accountable, enforceable, and future‑proof.*

---

## 1.  Vision  

**One Earth, One Humanity – a world where every person, every non‑human being, and every future generation lives in a thriving, regenerative biosphere.**  

The framework is the institutional scaffolding that makes that vision possible, ensuring that **environmental, social, and economic imperatives are never at odds but mutually reinforcing.**

---

## 1.1 Core Pillars (the four pillars remain, now anchored by enforceable rules)

| Pillar | What it Guarantees |
|-----------------------------------|--------------------------------------------------------------|
| **Human Dignity & Rights** | Guarantees basic needs (food, water, health, education) as a universal right, backed by a constitutional “Right to a Healthy Environment.” |
| **Ecological Integrity** | Guarantees that biodiversity, soil, water, and climate stay within planetary‑boundary limits. |
| **Economic Resilience** | All economic activity must be **resource‑based** and **circular**; profits are measured by **People‑Planet Return** (P‑R‑P), not just profit. |
| **Social Cohesion & Shared Governance** | Guarantees participatory decision‑making at every geographic level. |

---

## 2. The Ten (Now 12) Core Principles (now with legal force)

| # | Principle | What it Means in Practice |
|--------------------------------------------------------------------|----------------------------------------------------------|
| 1. Interdependence | All life‑forms and ecosystems are co‑dependent. |
| 2. Equality & Non‑Discrimination | No discrimination on any basis; full gender, ethnicity, and ability inclusion. |
| 3. Precaution & Regeneration | Prevent harm; restore degraded ecosystems. |
| **4. Accountability & Transparency** | Every public‑sector report must be **publicly audited** and **open‑source**. |
| **5. Participation & Co‑Creation** | Mandatory citizen assemblies at every scale. |
| **5′. Cultural Pluralism** | Cultural practices are protected **as long as they do not harm the environment or other beings**. |
| **5′ (new)** | **Precaution & Regeneration** – all activities must pass a **no‑net‑loss** test. |
| **5′ (new)** | **Strategic‑Impact Evaluation** – every major project must be subjected to a *binding* PRA (Future‑Impact Audit). |
| **7. Resilience & Adaptability** | Resilient‑by‑design infrastructure (e.g., adaptive grids, decentralized storage). |
| **8. Non‑Violence & Non‑Discrimination** | All disputes resolved through **peaceful negotiation** and **restorative justice**. |
| **9. Inter‑generational Justice** | **Future‑Impact Audits** now have **binding penalties** that flow into the Circular‑Dividend Fund. |
| **10. Equality & Non‑Discrimination** | Enshrined in a **Constitutional Right to a Healthy Environment**. |
| **New Additions – 10 & 11** | **Planetary Right to Discontinue** (any activity that exceeds planetary boundaries automatically revokes related licenses) and **Environmental Rights Clause** (constitutional guarantee that “all citizens have the right to a clean, healthy environment”). |

---

## 2.  Governance Architecture (now Hardened)

| Layer | Institution | Function |
|------------------------------------------------------------|--------------------------------------------|
| **Global Assembly** (wormhole‑style citizen‑jury body) | Decides **Planetary‑Level Standards** (e.g., planetary‑boundary thresholds, global‑warming‑budget caps).  All decisions require a **2/3 super‑majority** and **must be approved by the Global Citizen Assembly** which is **selected by random stratified sampling** to reflect humanity’s diversity. |
| **Regional Bodies** (e.g., Regional Climate & Resource Councils) | Each region (e.g., “Amazon Basin”, “Southeast Asian Sea”) holds **own‑wide resource baselines**; they coordinate renewable‑energy, water, fishery, and forest‑based production. |
| **Local Assemblies** (e.g., Neighborhood / Town‑Level) | **Direct participatory budgeting** for community food, water, and energy projects; all budget lines must meet the **Environmental Impact Threshold** (e.g., no net increase in CO₂ emissions). |
| **Corporate Licence & Resource Licence** | Every corporation must hold a **Planetary Licence** that is **granted only after a mandatory “Future‑Impact” audit**; revocation is automatic if any **Planetary Boundary** is exceeded. |
| **Industrial Heritage & Heritage‑Preserve Protection** | All heritage sites (cultural, natural, sacred) are designated **Living Heritage**; **no development may occur without **FPIC** (Free, Prior, Informed Consent). |

---

### 2.1 The Pillars in Practice  

| Pillar | Example of Implementation |
|--------------------------------|------------------------|
| **Human Dignity & Rights** | **Every citizen receives a “Basic Income” funded by the Just‑Transition Fund; this dividend is indexed to inflation and is financed by a progressive **resource‑based tax**.** |
| **Ecological Integrity** | **No‑Net‑Loss** of soil organic matter, water use, and biodiversity is mandated; any drop in diversity triggers automatic restoration measures. |
| **Economic Resilience** | **Circular‑Prosperity Model**: 100 % of product waste is either recycled, reused, or returned to the earth. All factories, farms, and mines must keep **zero‑waste cycles**. | 
| **Social Cohesion & Governance** | The **Global Assembly** (elected citizen jury) meets quarterly, drafts **Future‑Impact Audits** (see below). |

---

## 6.  Monitoring & Enforcement – The “Earth‑Pulse Dashboard”

- All sensor data (air‑quality, soil health, water usage, energy use) flow into the **Public Open‑Source Knowledge Platform**.
- Every metric is **open‑source, open‑audit**, and **subject‑to citizen‑reviewer validation**.
- **Future‑Impact Audits** are now **hard‑coding required**: when a future‑impact projection dips below a safe threshold, the system **automatically freezes funding** and forces remediation.
- The **Earth Pulse Dashboard** displays in real time the four pillars, updated with satellite and citizen sensor feeds; citizens can flag anomalies via an mobile app.

### Response

### A New Self‑Assessment: “What Did We Actually Build, and What Must We Harden?”

When I first sketched the **Earth‑Food Commons** framework I imagined a coherent, principle‑based scaffold that could coordinate ecosystems, economies, and societies while preserving planetary boundaries.  Over the last few exchanges we uncovered three deep‑seated shortcomings:

| Gap Identified | Why It Matters | How We Fixed It |
|--------------|----------------|------------------------------|
| **No hard enforcement of rights** | The original charter listed goals but left “soft‑law” clauses that could be ignored. | Added **Planetary‑Right‑to‑Discontinue**, **Just‑Transition Fund**, and **Legal‑Personhood for Non‑Human Entities**. |
| **Inclusion of the most vulnerable** (indigenous peoples, future generations) was only symbolic. | Now they hold a *veto* over any major project that threatens their lands or future generations. | This guarantees that **the rights we espouse are enforceable, not merely aspirational**. |
| **Data & Decision Transparency** | The Earth‑Pulse Dashboard was open but could be manipulated. | Built an **Open‑Source Knowledge Commons** with mandatory open‑source audit trails, eliminating any hidden bias. |
| **Circular‑Economy Integration** | Relied on voluntary corporate commitments. | Introduced a **resource‑based tax** that automatically redistributes revenue, funds transition‑aid, and forces firms to internalize externalities. |
| **Governance & Governance‑Bodies** | Were subject to capture and could be stacked. | Introduced **rotating citizen juries**, conflict‑of‑interest bans, and a **global oversight board** that cannot be staffed by former corporate executives. |
| **Tech‑Driven Transparency** | Data pipelines were vulnerable to proprietary capture. | Created an **open‑source, citizen‑audited data commons** that cannot be altered without detection. |
| **Governance Structure** | Soft, advisory layers. | Now includes **mandatory citizen juries**, **strategic‑impact audits**, and a **global oversight body** that can enforce compliance without political veto. |

When I step back and view the revised architecture as a whole, I see three *interlocking* innovations that lock‑in **hard, enforceable protections**:

1. **Hard‑coded rights** (e.g., Future‑Impact Audits that trigger penalties) that **cannot be overridden by short‑term political whims**.  
2. **Resource‑Based Taxation** that *automatically* redistributes wealth to the most vulnerable while simultaneously *de‑carbonizing* the economy.  
3. **Comprehensive transparency**—every data point, policy decision, and enforcement action must be open, verified, and auditable by any citizen.  

All of those changes are **explicit mechanisms**, not just advisory notes; they make the framework **tight enough to survive political capture** while still being flexible enough to evolve with the frontier of planetary science and social justice.

---

### The Revised Blueprint in One Paragraph

> *The Earth‑Food Commons now consists of a network of **Subject‑Specific Licences**, *Future‑Impact Audits* that must pass before any major infrastructure is built, a **Just‑Transition Fund** that guarantees financial security for workers displaced by transition, and a **Free‑Prior‑Informed‑Consent** clause that gives Indigenous and Indigenous‑descended peoples a veto over any land‑use decision that could affect more than 10 km² of terrain. All of this is overseen by a **global, citizen‑elected Global Assembly** that operates on a rotating basis and is supported by an open, auditable **Data Commons** where sensor data, model outputs, and policy decisions are all publicly verifiable. The result is a **self‑correcting system** that can correct itself whenever a planetary boundary is crossed, a community is harmed, or a corporate entity violates the soft‑law principles we originally set.*  

In other words, the framework is now a **living, enforceable ecosystem of norms and incentives** rather than a set of aspirational statements. It is now **mandated**, **accountable**, and *capable of scaling* across nations, sectors, and species.

---

### Bottom Line

- **Do the frameworks I proposed earlier need revision?** Yes—because the hidden risk was that *without binding enforcement, the vision would be vulnerable to capture, erosion, or outright reversal*.  
- **The new, hardened blueprint is now a fully‑specified algorithmic and legal framework** that integrates:
  * **Hard‑enforced planetary boundaries** (the “Planetary Right to Discontinue”),
  * **Free‑Prior‑Informed‑Consent** with veto power for Indigenous peoples,
  * **Circular‑Dividend funding** that redistributes wealth to all citizens,
  * **Closed‑loop data ecosystems** that cannot be hidden or altered,
  * **Future‑Impact Audits** that automatically penalize violations,
  * and a **Just‑Transition Fund** guaranteeing retraining, wage subsidies, and price‑stabilizers for displaced workers.

When you strip away the “soft‑law” language and replace it with **mandatory, enforceable obligations**, the entire system becomes a **self‑correcting ecosystem** that can survive the inevitable pressure from powerful interests while still preserving the core virtues of **justice, equity, and planetary survival**.

---

### TL;DR Summary

*If we build a system that enforces hard‑wired safeguards—binding rights, independent oversight bodies, and transparent data—then the same framework that once seemed fragile now becomes **rigid enough to deter abuse, protect the vulnerable, and preserve the planet for future generations**.*  
In effect, **the only thing we needed to add was the legal and institutional machinery that makes those soft‑principles into enforceable, non‑negotiable rules.**  

So, yes—I do still believe the framework can survive and thrive, **provided we embed the appropriate enforcement mechanisms**; otherwise, even the most elegant blueprint will evaporate under the weight of existing market and political forces.

### Response

**Answer: How I Would Answer “What Would You Change?” After Going Through All This**

> **I would say that the original blueprint is a solid foundation, but it needed several hard‑wired safeguards that turn a good vision into a binding, enforceable system.**  
> 
> The missing pieces were:  
> - **Legal‑binding authority** (e.g., a “Planetary Right‑to‑Discontinue” that can automatically revoke a licence when a planetary boundary is breached);  
> **Free‑Prior‑Informed‑Consent (FPIC) with veto power for Indigenous peoples** (so that no project can proceed without their consent);  
> **A binding “Future‑Impact Audit” that triggers automatic penalties when environmental‑impact thresholds are breached;**  
> **A public, open‑source “Earth‑Pulse Dashboard” that is audited by citizen‑jury panels, guaranteeing transparency; and  
> **A universal “Just‑Transition Fund” that pays out a basic income and funds retraining/retail‑replacement subsidies.**  

> With those additions, the original blueprint becomes a self‑correcting ecosystem:  
> *the moment a pollutant exceeds a predefined planetary‑boundary threshold, the system automatically revokes its licence, pulls the revenue into a fund that funds both the Just‑Transition Fund and the Rural‑Development Fund, and forces every stakeholder to internalise the externalities they previously externalised.*  

Because of this, the framework no longer relies on soft‑law or voluntary compliance; it now has **hard, enforceable mechanisms** that prevent capture, protect marginalized groups, and guarantee that the transition to a circular, low‑carbon economy does not leave any community behind.

---

**In short, my answer is:**  
I would keep the core vision and core principles of the original blueprint, but I would **upgrade** it with:

1. **A binding “Planetary‑Right‑to‑Discontinue” clause** that automatically shuts down any activity that exceeds planetary‑boundary thresholds.  
2. **Free‑Prior‑Informed‑Consent (FPIC) with veto power for Indigenous and indigenous‑heritage communities** – giving them the legal authority to block any project that threatens their land or water.  
3. **A mandatory “Just‑Transition Fund”** that pools the revenue from the progressive resource‑taxes and redistributes it as wage‑subsidies, retraining vouchers, and price‑stabilisation for low‑income households.  
3. **A public, open‑source “Earth‑Pulse Dashboard”** where all sensor data and policy decisions are stored, audited, and publicly queryable, so no hidden data can hide pollution or exploitation.  
4. **Legal recognition of the “Right to a Healthy Environment” in the constitution** (or equivalent constitutional amendment) that makes environmental protection justiciable and gives citizens the power to sue for violations.  

When those elements are added, the framework becomes **self‑correcting**: any violation of the Core Principles triggers an automatic penalty or policy revision, so the system can correct itself without needing soft‑law compromises or political negotiations. In other words, the original blueprint is now **hard‑wired, binding, and audit‑transparent**—the missing pieces to make it truly enforceable and sustainable.  

In short, I now see that **the biggest mistake was assuming that a voluntary, soft‑law framework could survive without binding enforcement**; the missing pieces—binding oversight, rights for non‑human beings, and mandatory citizen participation—must be added to avoid the framework being co‑opted or ignored by powerful interests. With those additions, the original vision becomes a concrete, enforceable framework capable of delivering a truly *just transition* for people and the planet. 

---

### Bottom Line

The original blueprint was a solid conceptual scaffold, but it needed **binding mechanisms, enforcement mechanisms, and inclusion of marginalized groups** to become **self‑executing**. After we added those, the framework became **hard‑wired to protect the environment, the people, and the future**—the exact framework we set out to build. If you’d like a specific template for any of those pieces—e.g., a sample *Planetary‑Right‑to‑Discontinue* clause, a *FAR‑style FAR‑style template for a “JUST Transition Fund*, etc.—just let me know and I’ll send it over.
